<p><b>Lagos</b> (<a href="/wiki/Nigerian_English" title="Nigerian English">Nigerian English</a>: <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/eɪ/: 'a' in 'face'">eɪ</span><span title="/ɡ/: 'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[9]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_language" title="Yoruba language">Yoruba</a>: <i lang="yo">Èkó</i>) is the largest city in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Africa_by_population" title="List of cities in Africa by population">second most populous city in Africa</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[11]</a></sup> with a population of 15.4 million as of 2015 within the city proper. 
Lagos was the national capital of Nigeria until December 1991 following the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a>'s decision to move their capital to <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a> in the centre of the country. The <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a> has a total <a href="/wiki/Population_and_housing_censuses_by_country" title="Population and housing censuses by country">population</a> of roughly 23.5 million as of 2018, making it <a href="/wiki/List_of_urban_areas_in_Africa_by_population" title="List of urban areas in Africa by population">the largest metropolitan area in Africa</a>. Lagos is a major African <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a> and is the economic hub of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a> and Nigeria at large. The city has been described as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cultural" title="Cultural">cultural</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial" title="Financial">financial</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Media_(communication)" title="Media (communication)">entertainment capital of Africa</a>, and is a significant influence on <a href="/wiki/Commerce" title="Commerce">commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Entertainment" title="Entertainment">entertainment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Technology" title="Technology">technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics" title="Politics">politics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>,  and <a href="/wiki/Fashion" title="Fashion">fashion</a>. Lagos is also among the top ten of the world's fastest-growing cities and urban areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[20]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> has the fourth-highest GDP in Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metropolitan_Lagos_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-metropolitan_Lagos-2">[2]</a></sup> and houses one of the <a href="/wiki/Apapa" title="Apapa">largest and busiest seaports</a> on the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-global_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-global-26">[24]</a></sup> The Lagos <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan</a> area is a major educational and cultural centre in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub Saharan Africa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lagos initially emerged as a home to the <a href="/wiki/Awori_tribe" title="Awori tribe">Awori</a> subgroup of the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a> and later emerged as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_city" title="Port city">port city</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benin_Empire" title="Benin Empire">Benin Empire</a> that originated on a collection of islands, which are contained in the present day Local Government Areas (<a href="/wiki/List_of_Lagos_State_local_government_areas_by_population" title="List of Lagos State local government areas by population">LGAs</a>) of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eti-Osa" title="Eti-Osa">Eti-Osa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amuwo-Odofin" title="Amuwo-Odofin">Amuwo-Odofin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apapa" title="Apapa">Apapa</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">islands</a> are separated by <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">creeks</a>, fringing the southwest mouth of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Lagoon" title="Lagos Lagoon">Lagos Lagoon</a>, while being protected from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> by <a href="/wiki/Barrier_island" title="Barrier island">barrier islands</a> and long <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sand_spit" title="Sand spit">sand spits</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Bar_Beach,_Lagos" title="Bar Beach, Lagos">Bar Beach</a>, which stretch up to 100 km (62 mi) east and west of the mouth. Due to rapid urbanization, the city expanded to the west of the lagoon to include areas in the present day <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Mainland" title="Lagos Mainland">Lagos Mainland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ajeromi-Ifelodun" title="Ajeromi-Ifelodun">Ajeromi-Ifelodun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surulere" title="Surulere">Surulere</a>. This led to the <a href="/wiki/Classification" title="Classification">classification</a> of Lagos into two main areas: the <a href="#Island">Island</a>, which was the original city of Lagos, and the <a href="#Mainland">Mainland</a>, which it has since expanded into.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_Case_Study_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_Case_Study-28">[26]</a></sup> This city area was governed directly by the Federal Government through the Lagos City Council, until the creation of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a> in 1967, which led to the splitting of Lagos city into the present day seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lagos_State_local_government_areas_by_population" title="List of Lagos State local government areas by population">Local Government Areas</a> (LGAs), and an addition of other towns (which now make up 13 LGAs) from the then <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Region,_Nigeria" title="Western Region, Nigeria">Western Region</a> to form the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>However, the state capital was later moved to <a href="/wiki/Ikeja" title="Ikeja">Ikeja</a> in 1976,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> and the federal capital moved to <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a> in 1991. Even though Lagos is still widely referred to as a city, the present-day Lagos, also known as "Metropolitan Lagos", and officially as "Lagos Metropolitan Area"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> is an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Urban_agglomeration" title="Urban agglomeration">urban agglomeration</a> or <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> consisting of 16 LGAs including Ikeja, the state capital of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metropolitan_Lagos_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-metropolitan_Lagos-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> This conurbation makes up 37% of Lagos State total land area, but houses about 85% of the state's total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metropolitan_Lagos_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-metropolitan_Lagos-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p><p>The exact population of Metropolitan Lagos is disputed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> In the 2006 federal census data, the conurbation had a population of about 8 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metropolitan_Lagos_population_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Metropolitan_Lagos_population-38">[36]</a></sup> However, the figure was disputed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagos_State_Government" title="Lagos State Government">Lagos State Government</a>, which later released its own population data, putting the population of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Metropolitan_Area_Transport_Authority" title="Lagos Metropolitan Area Transport Authority">Lagos Metropolitan Area</a> at approximately 16 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LGA_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-LGA-3">[note 1]</a></sup> Daily, the Lagos area is growing by some 3,000 people, or around 1.1 million annually, so the true population figure of the greater Lagos area in 2022 is roughly 28 million (up from some 23.5 million in 2018). Lagos may therefore have overtaken <a href="/wiki/Kinshasa" title="Kinshasa">Kinshasa</a> as Africa's most populous city. As of 2015, unofficial figures put the population of "Greater Metropolitan Lagos", which includes Lagos and its surrounding metro area, extending as far as into <a href="/wiki/Ogun_State" title="Ogun State">Ogun State</a>, at approximately 21 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metrolagospop_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-metrolagospop-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_sustainable_city_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_sustainable_city-40">[38]</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Lagos" title="History of Lagos">History of Lagos</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Lagos" title="Timeline of Lagos">Timeline of Lagos</a>.</div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_1929.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="468" data-file-width="612" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lagos_1929.png/220px-Lagos_1929.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lagos_1929.png/330px-Lagos_1929.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Lagos_1929.png/440px-Lagos_1929.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_1929.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Lagos in 1929</div></div></div>
<p>Lagos was originally inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Awori_tribe" title="Awori tribe">Awori</a> subgroup of the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba people</a> in the 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-afropolis_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-afropolis-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urban_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-urban-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> The Awori moved to an island now called Iddo and then to the larger Lagos Island. The Aworis who were predominantly fishermen and hunters, called it Oko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> Because the area was dominated by the then expansive Oyo Empire, they called it Eko, from the late 16th century to the mid-19th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[43]</a></sup> The name Eko was given to it by its first Awori traditional settlers, Oba Ado. Eko is still the native name for Lagos to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Lagos</i> (Portuguese for "lakes") was a name given to the settlement by the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a>. Throughout history, it was home to a number of warring ethnic Yoruba groups who had settled in the area. Following its early settlement by the Awori nobility, the state first came to the attention of the Portuguese in the 15th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>Portuguese explorer Rui de Sequeira visited the area in 1472, naming the area around the city <i>Lago de Curamo</i>, which means <i>Lake of Curamo</i>.
</p><p>In Britain's early 19th century fight against the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transatlantic_slave_trade" title="Transatlantic slave trade">transatlantic slave trade</a>, its <a href="/wiki/West_Africa_Squadron" title="West Africa Squadron">West Africa Squadron</a> or Preventative Squadron as it was also known, continued to pursue Portuguese, American, French and Cuban slave ships and to impose anti-slavery treaties with West African coastal chiefs with so much doggedness that they created a strong presence along the West African coast from Sierra Leone all the way to the Niger Delta (today's Nigeria) and as far south as Congo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith-1_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-1-48">[46]</a></sup> In 1849, Britain appointed <a href="/wiki/John_Beecroft" title="John Beecroft">John Beecroft</a> Consul of the Bights of Benin and Biafra, a position he held (along with his governorship of Fernando Po) until his death in 1854.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DNB_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-DNB-49">[47]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Duncan_(traveller_in_Africa)" title="John Duncan (traveller in Africa)">John Duncan</a> was appointed Vice Consul and was located at Wydah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Duncan_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Duncan-50">[48]</a></sup> At the time of Beecroft's appointment, the Kingdom of Lagos (under Oba Kosoko) was in the western part of the Consulate of the Bights of Benin and Biafra and was a key slave trading port.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-africa-51">[49]</a></sup> In 1851 and with pressure from liberated slaves who now wielded political and business influence, Britain intervened in Lagos in what is now known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Lagos" title="Bombardment of Lagos">Bombardment of Lagos</a> or Capture of Lagos<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africa_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-africa-51">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-british_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-british-52">[50]</a></sup> resulting in the installation of Oba <a href="/wiki/Akitoye" title="Akitoye">Akitoye</a> and the ouster of Oba <a href="/wiki/Kosoko" title="Kosoko">Kosoko</a>. Oba Akitoye then signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_Between_Great_Britain_and_Lagos,_1_January_1852" title="Treaty Between Great Britain and Lagos, 1 January 1852">Treaty between Great Britain and Lagos abolishing slavery</a>. The signing of the 1852 treaty ushered in the Consular Period in Lagos' history wherein Britain provided military protection for Lagos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reduction_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reduction-53">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[52]</a></sup>
</p><p>Following threats from Kosoko and the French who were positioned at Wydah, a decision was made by Lord <a href="/wiki/Henry_John_Temple,_3rd_Viscount_Palmerston" title="Henry John Temple, 3rd Viscount Palmerston">Palmerston</a> (British Prime Minister) who noted in 1861, "the expediency of losing no time in assuming the formal Protectorate of Lagos".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Smith-2_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-2-55">[53]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/William_McCoskry" title="William McCoskry">William McCoskry</a>, the Acting Consul in Lagos with Commander Bedingfield convened a meeting with Oba Dosunmu on 30 July 1861 aboard HMS <i>Prometheus</i> where Britain's intent was explained and a response to the terms were required by August 1861. Dosunmu resisted the terms of the treaty but under the threat to unleash a bombardment on Lagos by Commander Bedingfield, Dosunmu relented and signed the <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Treaty_of_Cession" title="Lagos Treaty of Cession">Lagos Treaty of Cession</a> on 6 August 1861.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-british_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-british-52">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Elebute_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Elebute-56">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Map.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="330" data-file-width="410" decoding="async" height="241" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Lagos_Map.PNG/300px-Lagos_Map.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/98/Lagos_Map.PNG 1.5x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Map.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Lagos' initial city boundaries, showing its contemporary districts. This definition is rarely used in the present day; the expanded metropolitan area is now a more accepted definition of Lagos.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lagos_Colony" title="Lagos Colony">Lagos</a> was declared a colony on 5 March 1862. The remainder of modern-day Nigeria was seized in 1887, and when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colony_and_Protectorate_of_Nigeria" title="Colony and Protectorate of Nigeria">Colony and Protectorate of Nigeria</a> was established in 1914, Lagos became its capital, continuing as such after the country's independence from Britain in 1960. Along with migrants from all over Nigeria and other West African nations were the returnee ex-slaves known as Creoles, who came from <a href="/wiki/Freetown" title="Freetown">Freetown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, Brazil and the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> to Lagos. The Creoles contributed to Lagos' modernisation and their knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_architecture" title="Portuguese architecture">Portuguese architecture</a> can still be seen from the architecture on Lagos Island. Since the 19th century, Lagos gradually transformed to a melting pot of Africans and Europeans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-urban_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-urban-7">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-google-60">[58]</a></sup> Railway links and telephone cables connecting Lagos to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> had been established by 1886.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bradt4_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-bradt4-61">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> Electric street lighting was introduced in the city in 1898.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Williamsguide_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Williamsguide-64">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Lagos experienced rapid growth throughout the 1960s and 1970s as a result of Nigeria's economic boom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conference_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conference-66">[64]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before the creation of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a> on 27 May 1967, Lagos, which was the country's capital had been administered directly by the Federal Government as a Federal Territory through the <i>Federal Ministry of Lagos Affairs</i>, while the Lagos City Council (LCC) governed the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup> Lagos, along with the towns from the then Western region (<a href="/wiki/Ikeja" title="Ikeja">Ikeja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agege" title="Agege">Agege</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mushin,_Lagos" title="Mushin, Lagos">Mushin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ikorodu" title="Ikorodu">Ikorodu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Epe,_Lagos_State" title="Epe, Lagos State">Epe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Badagry" title="Badagry">Badagry</a>), were eventually captured to create Lagos State.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup> Lagos city was split into the present day seven <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lagos_State_local_government_areas_by_population" title="List of Lagos State local government areas by population">Local Government Areas</a> (LGAs), while the other towns now make up 13 LGAs in the state. Lagos played the dual role of being the State and Federal Capital until 1976 when the state capital was moved to Ikeja. Lagos was adversely affected during Nigeria's military rule.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-first-67">[65]</a></sup> Also, on 12 December 1991, the seat of the Federal Government was also formally relocated to <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>. However, Lagos remains the financial centre of the country, and also grew to become the most populous conurbation in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lagos_State_Information_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-Lagos_State_Information-29">[27]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lagos is loosely classified into two main geographical areas—the "Island" and the "Mainland".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Lagos" title="Architecture of Lagos">Architecture of Lagos</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_Conservation_Center,_Canopy_walk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="2720" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg/220px-Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg/330px-Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg/440px-Lekki_Conservation_Center%2C_Canopy_walk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_Conservation_Center,_Canopy_walk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lekki_Conservation_Centre" title="Lekki Conservation Centre">Lekki Conservation Centre</a> canopy walk</div></div></div>
<p>Lagos has the tallest skyline in Nigeria. The architectural styles in Lagos are diverse and range from tropical and vernacular to colonial European and ultramodern buildings or a mixture. Brazilian style architecture brought by the creoles is evident in buildings such as Water House and  Shitta Bey Mosque.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup> Skyscrapers and most high rise buildings are centered on the islands, while the mainland has some high rise buildings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> In recent years, the Lagos State government has renovated existing parks and green areas, with a long-term goal of expansion. Many good quality buildings are interspersed across the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Island">Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Island is a loose geographical term that is used to define the area of Lagos that is separated from the "Mainland" by the main channel draining the lagoon into the Atlantic Ocean, which forms Lagos Harbour. The Island is mainly a collection of Islands that are separated from each other by creeks of varying sizes and are connected by bridges. The smaller sections of some creeks have been dredged and built over. This part of Lagos is the area where most business activities and entertainment events in Lagos take place. It also houses most of the upscale residential areas in Lagos. The Local Government Areas (LGAs) that are considered to be in the Island include <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eti-Osa" title="Eti-Osa">Eti-Osa</a>. The major upscale Island neighbourhoods within these LGAs include <a href="/wiki/Ikoyi" title="Ikoyi">Ikoyi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Island_(Nigeria)" title="Victoria Island (Nigeria)">Victoria Island</a>. Three major bridges join the Island to the Mainland. They are the <a href="/wiki/Carter_Bridge" title="Carter Bridge">Carter Bridge</a>, which starts from Iddo; the <a href="/wiki/Eko_Bridge" title="Eko Bridge">Eko Bridge</a> (formerly called the Second Mainland Bridge); and the <a href="/wiki/Third_Mainland_Bridge" title="Third Mainland Bridge">Third Mainland Bridge</a>, which passes through densely populated mainland suburbs to the Lagos Lagoon. The Ikoyi link bridge links Ikoyi and Lekki Phase 1, both of which are part of the Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup>
</p><p>Construction on the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Mainland_Bridge" title="Fourth Mainland Bridge">Fourth Mainland Bridge</a> will commence in 2022, according to Lagos State Governor, Babajide Sanwo-Olu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Lagos_Island">Lagos Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Lagos Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1936" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg/170px-2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg/255px-2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg/340px-2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2010_Lagos_Nigeria_5284107494.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lagos Marina</div></div></div>
<p>Lagos Island contains a <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> This district is characterized by high-rise buildings. The Island also contains many of the city's largest wholesale marketplaces (such as the popular <a href="/wiki/Idumota_Market" title="Idumota Market">Idumota</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balogun_Market" title="Balogun Market">Balogun Markets</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[79]</a></sup> It also has the National Museum of Nigeria, the Central Mosque, the Glover Memorial Hall, <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Church_of_Christ,_Lagos" title="Cathedral Church of Christ, Lagos">Christ's Church Cathedral (CMS)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oba_of_Lagos" title="Oba of Lagos">Oba</a>'s Palace (<a href="/wiki/Iga_Idunganran" title="Iga Idunganran">Iga Idunganran</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[80]</a></sup> Another major part of Lagos Island is Marina. It borders around the idumota and Balogun markets and houses major Banking institutions. Though formerly in a derelict condition, Lagos Island's <a href="/wiki/Tinubu_Square" title="Tinubu Square">Tinubu Square</a> is a site of historical importance; it was here that the Amalgamation Ceremony that unified the North and South <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> to form Nigeria took place in 1914.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Ikoyi">Ikoyi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Ikoyi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ikoyi" title="Ikoyi">Ikoyi</a></div>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:368px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ikoyi,_Lagos,_Nigeria.jpg" title="Aerial view of Ikoyi"><img alt="" data-file-height="3640" data-file-width="5464" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/360px-Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/540px-Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/720px-Ikoyi%2C_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg 2x" width="360"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ikoyi,_Lagos,_Nigeria.jpg" title="File:Ikoyi, Lagos, Nigeria.jpg"> </a></div>Aerial view of Ikoyi</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ikoyi" title="Ikoyi">Ikoyi</a> is situated on the eastern half of Lagos Island and joined to it by a <a href="/wiki/Landfill" title="Landfill">landfill</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> Ikoyi is also connected to Victoria Island by Falomo bridge, which carries the main road over Five Cowrie creek.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup> Falomo garden, a green public space which was developed by the state government in conjunction with Fidelity Bank in 2017, is located under the bridge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> Ikoyi housed the headquarters of the federal government of Nigeria and other buildings owned by the government, including the old federal secretariat complex. The complex today is on reestablishment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>In Ikoyi there are military and police barracks, a top-security prison and a federal high court of Nigeria. Ikoyi also has a number of hotels, night clubs, a recreational park and one of Africa's largest golf courses. Originally a <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">middle class</a> neighbourhood, in recent years, it has become a fashionable residential enclave for the <a href="/wiki/Upper_middle_class" title="Upper middle class">upper middle class</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Upper_class" title="Upper class">upper class</a>. There are also commercial activities in Ikoyi, which is spotted in an increasing number of offices, banks, and shopping complexes. The commercial section is concentrated in the South-West.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Victoria_Island">Victoria Island</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Victoria Island">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria_Island_(Nigeria)" title="Victoria Island (Nigeria)">Victoria Island (Nigeria)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1004_Flats,_Victoria_Island.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="1480" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg/220px-1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg/330px-1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg/440px-1004_Flats%2C_Victoria_Island.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1004_Flats,_Victoria_Island.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Victoria Island</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Civic_Towers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2265" data-file-width="4028" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Civic_Towers.jpg/220px-Civic_Towers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Civic_Towers.jpg/330px-Civic_Towers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Civic_Towers.jpg/440px-Civic_Towers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Civic_Towers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Civic Towers, Victoria Island, Lagos</div></div></div>
<p>Victoria Island with its annexe is situated to the south of Lagos Island  and known with a zip code of 101241<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> as assigned by NIPOST.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conference_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Conference-66">[64]</a></sup> It has expensive real estate properties and for that reason, many new luxury condos and apartments are blooming up everywhere.
Along with Ikoyi, Victoria Island occupies a major area in Lagos that boasts of several sizeable shopping districts. On its sea shore along the Atlantic front, there is environmentally reconstructed <a href="/wiki/Bar_Beach,_Lagos" title="Bar Beach, Lagos">Bar Beach</a>.
</p><p><b>Ajah/Lekki</b>
</p><p>The Lekki Peninsula shares some prestige with its Ikoyi and Victoria Island neighbours. Development has stretched the piece of land further such that the Ibeju axis, though closer to Epe (which is literally on the outskirts of Lagos) is almost always described as part of Lekki.  The expanse of land starts from the Lekki toll gate, which was the focal stage of the famous #EndSars protest in October 2019, and ends in Ibeju-Lekki and boasts of communities slowly inching their way to suburb status such as <a href="/wiki/Ajah,_Lagos" title="Ajah, Lagos">Ajah</a>, Awoyaya, Sangotedo, Abijo and Eputu. There's quite a bit of places to see – the Lekki Conservation Centre; The Novare Mall; The Lekki Free Trade Zone – Dangote, Africa's richest man is building his refinery in this FTZ; Lagos Business School; Eleko Beach; Elegushi Beach; La Camaigne Tropicana – a beach/tourist getaway, Pan-Atlantic University. The area even boasts of a Catholic monastery.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Iddo">Iddo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Iddo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Across the main channel of the lagoon from Lagos Island, there is a smaller settlement called <a href="/wiki/Iddo_Island" title="Iddo Island">Iddo</a>. Iddo is also <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Terminus_railway_station" title="Lagos Terminus railway station">a railroad terminus</a> and it is now situated in the Lagos Mainland Local Government Area after it was connected to the Mainland like a peninsula.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[87]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainland">Mainland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mainland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A huge population of Lagosians also live on the Lagos Mainland, and most industries are located there. The Mainland is known for its music and nightlife, which used to be located in areas around <a href="/wiki/Yaba,_Lagos" title="Yaba, Lagos">Yaba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surulere" title="Surulere">Surulere</a>. However, in recent years more night clubs have sprung up on the Island, making the Island (particularly Victoria Island, Ikate and Lekki Phase 1) the main nightlife attractions. Mainland LGAs include <a href="/wiki/Surulere" title="Surulere">Surulere</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apapa" title="Apapa">Apapa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Mainland" title="Lagos Mainland">Lagos Mainland</a>. Metropolitan Lagos suburban LGAs include: <a href="/wiki/Agege" title="Agege">Agege</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amuwo_Odofin" title="Amuwo Odofin">Amuwo Odofin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mushin,_Lagos" title="Mushin, Lagos">Mushin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oshodi-Isolo" title="Oshodi-Isolo">Oshodi-Isolo</a> and Ikeja (site of <a href="/wiki/Murtala_Muhammed_International_Airport" title="Murtala Muhammed International Airport">Murtala Muhammed International Airport</a> and the capital of Lagos State).
</p><p>Major areas on the Mainland include <a href="/wiki/Ebute_Metta" title="Ebute Metta">Ebute Metta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yaba,_Lagos" title="Yaba, Lagos">Yaba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ejigbo,_Lagos" title="Ejigbo, Lagos">Ejigbo</a>. Some rivers, like <a href="/wiki/Badagry" title="Badagry">Badagry</a> Creek, flow parallel to the coast for some distance before exiting through the sand bars to the sea.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Lagos experiences a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">tropical savanna climate</a> (<i>Aw</i>) according to the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, as there are four months under 60 mm or 2.4 in of rain, and annual rainfall is not nearly high enough for <a href="/wiki/Tropical_monsoon_climate" title="Tropical monsoon climate">tropical monsoon</a> classification. The wet season starts in March and ends in October, while the dry season starts in November and ends in February. The wettest month is June with precipitation total 315.5 mm or 12.42 in, while the driest month is January with precipitation total 13.2 mm or 0.52 in.
</p><p>Located near the equator, Lagos has only a slight seasonal temperature variation, with mean high temperatures ranging from 28.3 to 32.9 °C (82.9 to 91.2 °F). Lagos shares the seasons of the Southern Hemisphere, with highest temperatures in March with a daily range from 32.9 to 24.1 °C (91.2 to 75.4 °F), and least hot temperatures in August ranging from 28.3 to 21.8 °C (82.9 to 71.2 °F).
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In terms of administration, Lagos is not a single <a href="/wiki/Municipality" title="Municipality">municipality</a> and therefore has no overall city administration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> The geographical city limits of Metropolitan Lagos comprise 16 of the 20 Local Government Areas of Lagos State. The latter entity provides overall government for the metropolitan region. The former Municipality of Lagos, which covered Lagos Island, Ikoyi, and Victoria Island as well as some mainland territory, was managed by the Lagos City Council (LCC), but it was disbanded in 1976 and divided into several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Government_Areas_in_Nigeria" title="Local Government Areas in Nigeria">Local Government Areas</a> (most notably Lagos Island LGA, <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Mainland" title="Lagos Mainland">Lagos Mainland LGA</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eti-Osa" title="Eti-Osa">Eti-Osa LGA</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>The mainland beyond the Municipality of Lagos, on the other hand, included several separate towns and settlements such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mushin,_Nigeria" title="Mushin, Nigeria">Mushin</a>, Ikeja and Agege. In the wake of the 1970s Nigerian oil boom, Lagos experienced a population explosion, untamed economic growth, and unmitigated rural migration. This caused the outlying towns and settlements to develop rapidly, thus forming the present day "Lagos Metropolitan Area", also known as "Metropolitan Lagos". The history of Lagos is still evidenced in the layout of the LGAs that display the unique identities of the cultures that created them.
</p><p>By 2006, the metro area around Lagos had extended beyond Lagos State's boundaries and attained a <a href="/wiki/Megacity" title="Megacity">megacity</a> status. This much larger area is referred to as "Greater Metropolitan Lagos" or "Lagos Megacity Region", which is a continuous built up land area of an additional 1,535.4 square kilometres (592.8 <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">square miles</a>), in LGAs situated next to Lagos' eastern and western city limits in Lagos State, and also beyond its northern limits, spilling into some LGAs in adjoining <a href="/wiki/Ogun_State" title="Ogun State">Ogun State</a>. Ogun State LGAs that have become part of Greater Metropolitan Lagos include <a href="/wiki/Obafemi_Owode" title="Obafemi Owode">Obafemi Owode</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sagamu" title="Sagamu">Sagamu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ifo" title="Ifo">Ifo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ado-Odo/Ota" title="Ado-Odo/Ota">Ado-Odo/Ota</a> and part of <a href="/wiki/Ewekoro" title="Ewekoro">Ewekoro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_sustainable_city_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_sustainable_city-40">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="width:650px; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:552px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="473" data-file-width="898" decoding="async" height="290" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png/550px-Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png/825px-Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png 2x" width="550"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Local_Government_Areas_of_Lagos.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the 16 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Local_Government_Areas_in_Nigeria" title="Local Government Areas in Nigeria">LGAs</a> making up Lagos Metropolitan Area</div></div></div>
<p>Today, the word <i>Lagos</i> most often refers to the urban area, called "Metropolitan Lagos" in Nigeria, which includes both the islands of the former municipality of Lagos and the mainland suburbs. Lagos State government is responsible for some of the utilities including roads and transportation, power, water, health and education. Metropolitan Lagos extends over 16 of the 20 LGAs of Lagos State, and contains about 85% of the population of Lagos State, including some semi-rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-METRO_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-METRO-98">[96]</a></sup> Lagos has a considerable number of high-rise buildings that dominate its skyline. Most of the tall buildings are located in the downtown Central Business District.
</p><p>Lagos was formerly the capital city of Nigeria, but it has since been replaced by <a href="/wiki/Abuja" title="Abuja">Abuja</a>. Abuja officially became the capital of Nigeria on 12 December 1991, although the decision to move the federal capital had been made in now Act no. 6 of 1976. Lagos is also home to the High Court of the <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State_Judiciary" title="Lagos State Judiciary">Lagos State Judiciary</a>, housed in an old colonial building on Lagos Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Census_data_for_Lagos">Census data for Lagos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Census data for Lagos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Although the 2006 National Population Census of Nigeria credited the metropolitan area with a population figure of 7,937,932, the figure is at variance with some projections by the UN and other population agencies and groups worldwide. The population figure of <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a> given by the Lagos State Government is 17,553,924. That figure was based on claimed conducted enumeration for social planning by the Lagos State Government "parallel census" and it believes that since the inhabitants of the metropolitan area of Lagos constitute 88% of the Lagos State population, the population of metropolitan Lagos is about 15.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup>
</p><p>A rejoinder to Lagos State Government views<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> concluded that Lagos State concealed the fact that the population projection, for Lagos Urban Agglomeration by the UN agencies had been revised downwards substantially as early as 2003. It failed to interpret the two most important and fairly representative and reliable secondary data sets already in public domain, the National Identity Card Scheme and the 2003 Voters Registration figures from INEC. The figures for 2007 Voters Registration by INEC were an act subsequent to the release of the provisional census results and comprehensively corroborate, vindicate and validate the population figures in no uncertain terms.
According to the official results of the 2006 census, there were 8,048,430 inhabitants in Metropolitan Lagos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metropolitan_Lagos_population_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-Metropolitan_Lagos_population-38">[36]</a></sup> This figure was lower than anticipated, and has created controversy in Nigeria. Lagos Island, the central Local Government Area and historic centre of Metropolitan Lagos, had a population of 212,700 at the 2006 Census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Market_in_Lagos,_Nigeria.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="582" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/220px-Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/330px-Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg/440px-Market_in_Lagos%2C_Nigeria.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Market_in_Lagos,_Nigeria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lagos market scene</div></div></div>
<p>Authorities of Lagos State have attacked the results of the 2006 census, accusing the Nigerian National Population Commission of having undercounted the population of the state. This accusation is denied by the National Population Commission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[102]</a></sup> A study found that research carried out by Africapolis (the African subsidiary of e-Geopolis backed by the <a href="/wiki/French_Development_Agency" title="French Development Agency">Agence française de développement</a>), in addition to the cross-referencing of official figures with more scientific independent research concluded that the 2006 census figures for Lagos State of about 9 million were valid and that the state's own assessments are inflated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lagos is, by most estimates, one of the fastest-growing cities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africareport_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-africareport-106">[104]</a></sup> Lagos is currently experiencing a population increase of about 275,000 persons per annum. In 1999 the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> predicted that the city's metropolitan area, which had only about 290,000 inhabitants in 1950, would exceed 20 million by 2010 and thus become one of the ten most populated cities in the world.
</p><p>
There is a huge spectrum of wealth distribution among the people that reside in Lagos. It ranges from the very wealthy to the very poor. Lagos has attracted many young people and families seeking a better life from all other parts of Nigeria and beyond<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-first-67">[65]</a></sup> and this has also contributed to its cosmopolitan status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[109]</a></sup> </p><table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:none;clear:none;margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa
