<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Apapa_port.lagos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Apapa_port.lagos.jpg/220px-Apapa_port.lagos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Apapa_port.lagos.jpg/330px-Apapa_port.lagos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Apapa_port.lagos.jpg/440px-Apapa_port.lagos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Apapa_port.lagos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apapa port</div></div></div>
<p>The city of Lagos is a major economic focal point in Nigeria, generating around 10% of the country's GDP. Most commercial and financial business is carried out in the <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> situated on the island. This is also where most of the country's commercial banks, financial institutions and major corporations are headquartered. Lagos is also the major Information Communications and Telecommunications (ICT) hub of West Africa and potentially, the biggest ICT market in the continent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[112]</a></sup> Lagos is developing a <a href="/wiki/24/7_service" title="24/7 service">24-hour economy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nightlife_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-nightlife-116">[114]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ports">Ports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1236" data-file-width="1913" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg/220px-Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg/330px-Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg/440px-Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Free-Trade-Zone-Lekki-English2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lagos, its ports, airports, free trade zone and light rail system</div></div></div>
<p>The Port of Lagos is Nigeria's leading <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">port</a> and one of the largest and busiest in Africa. Due to the large urban population, Lagos is categorized as a medium-port megacity using the Southampton System for port-city classification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> It is administered by the <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_Ports_Authority" title="Nigerian Ports Authority">Nigerian Ports Authority</a>. The following types of vessels regularly call at the port of Lagos: Fishing vessels (18%), container ships (14%), oil/chemical tankers (13%), bulk carriers (12%), offshore supply vessels (5%). The maximum length of vessels that have called at this port is 279 meters. The maximum draught is 13.5 m. The maximum carrying capacity is 113,306 t.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup>
</p><p>The port features a railhead. It is split into three main sections. The largest terminal is located in the Apapa district (Apapa Quays). This is where mainly general cargo is handled. Among other things, Apapa is home to a container port owned by the Danish company A. P. Møller-Mærsk, worth over one billion U.S. dollars. The next largest terminal is located on Tin Can Island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> Containers and bulk cargo are handled here. The storage capacity of the silos is 28,000 tons of grain transported by Fleetwood Transportation. The terminal handles wheat, corn and malt, and can receive about 4000 tons of grain daily. The port facilities can handle vessels with a capacity of about 30,000 tons. There is also a grain bagging facility on the site. Third is the Lagos oil port north of Apapa Quays.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Entertainment_industry_and_media">Entertainment industry and media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Entertainment industry and media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Nigeria" title="Cinema of Nigeria">Cinema of Nigeria</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg"><img alt="Nollywood" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="940" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg/220px-Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg/330px-Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg/440px-Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Future_Ambassadors_movie_onset.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Filming</div></div></div>
<p>Lagos is the center of the West African film, music, and TV industries. The film industry in the Surulere locality ranks second or third in the world, ahead of or behind Hollywood, depending on the survey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> PricewaterhouseCoopers Int. forecasts that the Nigerian entertainment industry will grow 85% to $15 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup>
Since the success of the Nigerian thriller "The Figurine", Nigerian film has increasingly turned to high quality productions that are also commercially successful. This, in turn, has led to consistently new box office revenue records in Nigeria (2009's "The Figurine," 2013's "Half of a Yellow Sun," 2016's "The Wedding Party").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lekki_Free_Trade_Zone">Lekki Free Trade Zone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lekki Free Trade Zone">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg/220px-Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg/330px-Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg/440px-Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_free_trade_zone.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance of the Lekki Free Trade Zone</div></div></div>
<p>Lekki Free Trade Zone (Lekki FTZ) is a free zone situated at the eastern part of Lekki, which covers a total area of about 155 square kilometres. The first phase of the zone has an area of 30 square kilometres, with about 27 square kilometres for urban construction purposes, which would accommodate a total resident population of 120,000. According to the Master Plan, the free zone will be developed into a new modern city within a city with integration of industries, commerce and business, real estate development, warehousing and logistics, tourism, and entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China-Africa_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-China-Africa-124">[122]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lekki FTZ is divided into three functional districts; the residential district in the north, industrial district in the middle and commercial trading/warehousing &amp; logistics district in the southeast. The "sub-centre" located in the south of the Zone is to be developed first. The region is close to the customs supervisory area, and it is mainly for commercial trading, logistics and warehousing operations. The second phase is located in the north of the Zone adjacent to E9 Road (Highway) which will serve as <a href="/wiki/Central_business_district" title="Central business district">central business district</a> of the free zone. The area along E2 Road will be developed for financial and commercial businesses, estate properties &amp; supporting facilities, high-end production service industries and so on, which will link it to the sub-centre the Zone. The area along E4 Road will be utilized mainly for the development of logistics and industrial manufacturing/processing. A number of connection axes are also planned in-between the principal axis and the sub-axis, with multi-functional service nodes to serve the whole of Lekki FTZ.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China-Africa_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-China-Africa-124">[122]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dangote_Refinery" title="Dangote Refinery">Dangote Refinery</a> is currently being built in the Lekki Free Zone.
</p><p>In the start-up area of the Lekki Free Trade Zone, there will be a Commercial &amp; Logistics Park which will cover a total area of 1.5 square kilometres. The Park is planned to be multi-functional with the integration of commerce, trading, warehousing, and exhibition. According to the Site Plan of the park, large construction works will be built in the park, including the "international commodities &amp; trade centre", the "international exhibition &amp; conversation centre", industrial factory workshops, logistics warehouses, office buildings, hotels and residential apartment buildings, amongst others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-China-Africa_124-2"><a href="#cite_note-China-Africa-124">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_refinery">Oil refinery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Oil refinery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dangote_Refinery" title="Dangote Refinery">Dangote Refinery</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1887" data-file-width="1946" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg/220px-Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg/330px-Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg/440px-Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Column-Dangote-refinery.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distilling column of the Dangote refinery in compare to a <a href="/wiki/Saturn_(rocket_family)" title="Saturn (rocket family)">Saturn rocket</a></div></div></div>
<p>Until now, paradoxically, oil <i>exporter</i> Nigeria had to <i>import</i> its oil derivatives (mainly gasoline) and oil processing by-products such as polypropylene. For this reason, the Dangote Group built an <a href="/wiki/Dangote_Refinery" title="Dangote Refinery">oil refinery</a> in the Lekki district, which is expected to be operational in 2022 (as of December 2021).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> Job advertisements for this were placed in November 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> The refinery is expected to process 650,000 barrels of oil per day when fully operational, and 327, 000 barrels of gasoline, 244,000 barrels of diesel, 56,000 barrels of aviation fuel, 800 megatons of propane, 2,500 megatons of polypropylene, and 100 megatons of sulfur.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> 9,000 direct jobs and 25,000 indirect jobs will be created by the refinery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The oil industry has been a major polluter of Lagos' water sources for decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_companies">Software companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Software companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Software companies in Lagos work mainly in the telecommunications, banking and education/employment services sectors. They are concentrated in the Lekki and Ikeja districts.
</p><p>MTN maintains the first and still predominant 4G network in Nigeria. Airtel is another 4G provider. 9Mobile and Dataflex are Internet providers. Flutterwave is in the virtual bank card business. Opay is a platform for online bookings. Paystack is used by Nigerians who regularly receive payments from abroad. Andela trains software engineers and places them in the Nigerian job market. ULesson maintains a platform on which secondary school learning content is presented. Hotels.ng allows hotel bookings to be made throughout Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Yaba" title="Yaba">Yaba</a> has increasingly been a focal point with several software companies and engineering services companies set up around <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lagos" title="University of Lagos">University of Lagos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaba_College_of_Technology" title="Yaba College of Technology">Yabatech</a> communities including Flutterwave and Andela. Several start up incubators and entrepreneurs hubs are also located in the area which is sometimes called Yabacon valley in reference to <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Automotive_Industry">Automotive Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Automotive Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Nigeria" title="Automotive industry in Nigeria">Automotive industry in Nigeria</a></div>
<p>Former Mercedes manager Oluwatobi Ajayi founded "Nord Automobiles Ltd" in the Sangotedo district in 2018. He benefited from the decline of the naira, which made importing vehicles unaffordable for many Nigerians. Nord has two assembly plants in Lagos: a 2,100 m<sup>2</sup> plant in Sangotedo, where all eight models are currently assembled; the second 5,400 m2 plant in Epe is still under construction. Once completed, assembly of the models will be moved to the new plant, while component manufacturing will take place in Sangotedo. The company currently manufactures its own plastic parts and plans to add steel stamping in the future. "In the new plant, we could produce about 1,000 vehicles per month. But the market is not yet big enough to justify assembly on that scale. We've only been selling officially since September, and our orders are increasing by 20% to 30% per month," Ajayi adds. The company offers eight different models, with the 3-ton pickup, the Nord Tank, being the most popular. The others are the Nord Max (2.6-ton pickup), Nord A3 (sedan), Nord A5 (luxury SUV), Nord Flit minibus, Nord Yarn and Nord Tripper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fertiliser">Fertiliser</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Fertiliser">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertiliser</a> production plant was commissioned in the Lekki Free Trade Zone on May 3, 2022. It will produce 3 million tonnes of fertiliser a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-african.business_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-african.business-140">[138]</a></sup> Since Russian fertiliser is refrained from coming onto the world market due to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukraine_war" title="Ukraine war">Ukraine war 2022</a>, Nigeria fills a gap in the market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-african.business_140-1"><a href="#cite_note-african.business-140">[138]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pharmaceutical_industry">Pharmaceutical industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Pharmaceutical industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_,_Lagos_state.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg/220px-Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg/330px-Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg/440px-Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_%2C_Lagos_state.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buying_drugs_from_a_Pharmacy_in_Epe_,_Lagos_state.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pharmacy in <a href="/wiki/Epe,_Lagos_State" title="Epe, Lagos State">Epe</a></div></div></div>
<p>Nigeria hosts about 60 percent of the pharmaceutical production capacity in Africa (status 2022).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> The larger pharmaceutical companies in Nigeria are located in the North of Lagos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[140]</a></sup> <i>Emzor Pharmaceutical Industries Ltd</i> appears to be the pharmaceutical producer with the most employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup> Next in line are <i>Fidson Healthcare Plc</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> <i>May &amp; Baker Nig. Plc</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[143]</a></sup> and <i>Swiss Pharma Nigeria</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[144]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_situation">Social situation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Social situation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Oil export revenues have led to a general increase in prices and cost of living, making Lagos the most expensive city in Nigeria. Despite its oil wealth, long queues are commonplace at the country's gas stations due to gasoline shortages. Yet the city remains more or less functional, and rapid growth is producing intact infrastructures even without government intervention-despite what the West sees as a chaotic picture<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>. Change and permeability characterize urban coexistence. One room is occupied by an average of four people, and life takes place primarily on the streets.
During rush hour between the center and the residential areas, the main traffic routes are transformed into marketplaces. After improvements in living conditions, the 1990s with their economic and political crises led to mass impoverishment in Lagos as well.
In a 2018 ranking of cities by quality of life, Lagos ranked 212th among 231 cities surveyed worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[145]</a></sup>
Lagos has been ranked as one of the most expensive cities in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[151]</a></sup> In some parts of Lagos, residents have one of the highest standards of living in Nigeria and in Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[153]</a></sup> At the same time, a sizable proportion of the residents live in slums without access to piped water and sanitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[157]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[158]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_film_industry">Music and film industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Music and film industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lagos is famous throughout Africa for its music scene. Lagos has a vibrant nightlife<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nightlife_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-nightlife-116">[114]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-161">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[160]</a></sup> and has given birth to a variety of styles such as <a href="/wiki/Sakara_music" title="Sakara music">Sakara music</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nigerian_hip_hop" title="Nigerian hip hop">Nigerian hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Highlife" title="Highlife">highlife</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B9j%C3%BA_music" title="Jùjú music">juju</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fuji_music" title="Fuji music">fuji</a> and <a href="/wiki/Afrobeats" title="Afrobeats">Afrobeats</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MUSIC_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-MUSIC-163">[161]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lagos is the centre of the Nigerian movie industry, often referred to as '<a href="/wiki/Nollywood" title="Nollywood">Nollywood</a>'. Idumota market on Lagos Island is the primary distribution centre. Many films are shot in the <a href="/wiki/Festac_Town" title="Festac Town">Festac</a> area of Lagos, where the <a href="/wiki/World_Festival_of_Black_Arts" title="World Festival of Black Arts">World Festival of Black Arts</a> was held.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOLLYWOOD_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOLLYWOOD-164">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p>Iganmu is home to the primary centre for the performing arts and artistes in Nigeria: the <a href="/wiki/National_Arts_Theatre" title="National Arts Theatre">National Arts Theatre</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/James_Brown" title="James Brown">James Brown</a> performed in Lagos in 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[163]</a></sup> With his band <i><a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney_and_Wings" title="Paul McCartney and Wings">Wings</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a> recorded his fifth post-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beatles" title="Beatles">Beatles</a> album, <i><a href="/wiki/Band_on_the_Run" title="Band on the Run">Band on the Run</a></i>, in an <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a> studio in Lagos in August and September 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[164]</a></sup> Other foreign musicians who have also performed in the city include <a href="/wiki/Sean_Paul" title="Sean Paul">Sean Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[165]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, <a href="/wiki/Akon" title="Akon">Akon</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jarule" title="Jarule">Jarule</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(singer)" title="Usher (singer)">Usher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaggy_(musician)" title="Shaggy (musician)">Shaggy</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[166]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R_Kelly" title="R Kelly">R Kelly</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cardi_B" title="Cardi B">Cardi B</a>, <a href="/wiki/Migos" title="Migos">Migos</a> especially during the <a href="/wiki/Star_Mega_Jam" title="Star Mega Jam">Star Mega Jam</a>; <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Legend" title="John Legend">John Legend</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men" title="Boyz II Men">Boyz II Men</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/T-Pain" title="T-Pain">T-Pain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_McKnight" title="Brian McKnight">Brian McKnight</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JayZ" title="JayZ">JayZ</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[169]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_J._Blige" title="Mary J. Blige">Mary J. Blige</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[170]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ciara" title="Ciara">Ciara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keri_Hilson" title="Keri Hilson">Keri Hilson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lauryn_Hill" title="Lauryn Hill">Lauryn Hill</a>, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[172]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_squares">Parks and squares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Parks and squares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2872" data-file-width="3828" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg/220px-Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg/330px-Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg/440px-Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tree_Growing_on_Fence_of_Freedom_Park_in_Lagos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tree growing in Freedom Park</div></div></div>
<p><b>Freedom Park</b> is a memorial and leisure park area in the middle of downtown Lagos in <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> which was formerly Her Majesty's Broad Street Prison. It was designed by the Architect Theo Lawson.
</p><p>The Park was constructed to preserve the history and cultural heritage of Nigerians. Monuments in the park reveal the Lagos colonial heritage and history of Her Majesty's Broad Street prisons. It was built to commemorate the 50th anniversary independence celebration in October, 2010. The Park serves as a National Memorial, a Historical landmark, a Cultural site, Arts and Recreation centre.
</p><p>The park, which is now a serene abode for individuals, visitors' collective contemplation and interaction is open to the public every day. Today, freedom park has become a venue for diverse social events and recreational entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[173]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[174]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg/220px-Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg/330px-Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg/440px-Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tinubu_Square_Inside.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tinubu Square</div></div></div>
<p><b>Tinubu Square</b> (formerly <b>Independence Square</b>), is an open space landmark located in <a href="/wiki/Broad_Street,_Lagos" title="Broad Street, Lagos">Broad Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lagos_State" title="Lagos State">Lagos State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> named after the <a href="/wiki/Yoruba_people" title="Yoruba people">Yoruba</a> slave trader, merchant, and aristocrat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madam_Efunroye_Tinubu" title="Madam Efunroye Tinubu">Madam Efunroye Tinubu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[175]</a></sup> It used to be called <i>Ita Tinubu</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Yemitan1987_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-Yemitan1987-178">[176]</a></sup> before it was named <i>Independence Square</i> by leaders of the <a href="/wiki/First_Nigerian_Republic" title="First Nigerian Republic">First Nigerian Republic</a> after Nigerian independence and subsequently <i>Tinubu Square</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-the_nation_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-the_nation-179">[177]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <b>Tafawa Balewa Square, (TBS)</b> is a 14.5-hectare (35.8-acre) ceremonial ground (originally called "Race Course") in <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island" title="Lagos Island">Lagos Island</a>, Lagos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-building_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-building-180">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[179]</a></sup> The entrance to the square has gigantic sculptures of four white horses hovering above the gate and seven red eagles, which are symbols from the national emblem signifying Strength and Dignity respectively. Other monuments in the square include the Remembrance Arcade <a class="external text" href="http://ng.geoview.info/remembrance_arcade,198984537w" rel="nofollow">1</a>(with memorials to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nigerian_civil_war" title="Nigerian civil war">Nigerian civil war</a> victims) and the 26-storey Independence House, built in 1963 which was for a long time, the tallest building in Nigeria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-building_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-building-180">[178]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg/220px-A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg/330px-A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg/440px-A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_side_view_of_the_National_Stadium.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Lagos" title="National Stadium, Lagos">National Stadium</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is Lagos' most popular sport. Prominent Lagos football clubs include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bridge_Boys_F.C." title="Bridge Boys F.C.">Bridge Boys F.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/MFM_F.C." title="MFM F.C.">MFM F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_Bank_F.C." title="First Bank F.C.">First Bank</a>: both play in <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_National_League" title="Nigeria National League">Nigeria National League</a>, the second tier of Nigerian football.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG/220px-Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG/330px-Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG/440px-Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Black_Heritage_Festival_Parade.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Lagos Black Heritage Festival Parade, 2012</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_national_football_team" title="Nigeria national football team">Nigeria national football team</a>, also known as the Super Eagles, used to play almost all of their home games in Lagos at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagos_National_Stadium" title="Lagos National Stadium">National Stadium</a> in Surulere; much later, games were played at the then New <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Abuja_National_Stadium" title="Abuja National Stadium">Abuja National Stadium</a> in Abuja for sometime; however, games are now mostly played at the newer <a href="/wiki/Godswill_Akpabio_International_Stadium" title="Godswill Akpabio International Stadium">Godswill Akpabio International Stadium</a> in Uyo, which is the default home of the Super Eagles. Lagos also hosted the 2nd All-African games in 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1454" data-file-width="2456" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg/220px-Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg/330px-Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg/440px-Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lekki_Beach_in_Lagos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lekki Beach in Lagos</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg/220px-The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg/330px-The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg/440px-The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Cathedral_Church_of_Christ_Marina..jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Cathedral Church of Christ Marina on Lagos Island</div></div></div>
<p>Lagos, subsequent to the re-modernization project achieved by the previous administration of Governor Raji Babatunde Fashola, is gradually becoming a major tourist destination, being one of the largest cities in Africa and in the world. Lagos is currently taking steps to become a <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> and is rated as Beta − by the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[183]</a></sup> The 2009 Eyo carnival (a yearly festival originated from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iperu_Remo" title="Iperu Remo">Iperu Remo</a>, Ogun State), which took place on 25 April, was a step toward world city status. Currently, Lagos is primarily known as a business-oriented and a fast-paced community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-METRO_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-METRO-98">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lagos has become an important location for African and <a href="/wiki/Black_people" title="Black people">Black</a> cultural identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[184]</a></sup> Many festivals are held in Lagos; festivals vary in offerings each year and may be held in different months. Some of the festivals are <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20180820075714/http://www.festacfoodfair.com/" rel="nofollow">Festac Food Fair held in Festac</a> Town Annually, Eyo Festival, <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20181102044321/http://lagosblackheritagefestival.com/" rel="nofollow">Lagos Black Heritage Carnival</a>, Lagos Carnival, Eko International Film Festival, Lagos Seafood Festac Festival, LAGOS PHOTO Festival and the Lagos Jazz Series, which is a unique franchise for high-quality live music in all genres with a focus on jazz. Established in 2010, the popular event takes place over a 3–5 day period at selected high quality outdoor venues. The music is as varied as the audience itself and features a diverse mix of musical genres from rhythm and blues to soul, <a href="/wiki/Afrobeat" title="Afrobeat">Afrobeat</a>, hip hop, bebop, and traditional jazz. The festivals provide entertainment of dance and song to add excitement to travelers during a stay in Lagos.
</p><p>Lagos has a number of sandy beaches by the Atlantic Ocean, including <a href="/wiki/Elegushi_Beach" title="Elegushi Beach">Elegushi Beach</a> and Alpha Beach. Lagos also has a number of private beach resorts including Inagbe Grand Beach Resort and several others in the outskirts.
</p><p>Lagos has a variety of hotels ranging from three star to five star hotels, with a mixture of local hotels such as <a href="/wiki/Eko_Hotels_and_Suites" title="Eko Hotels and Suites">Eko Hotels and Suites</a>, <a href="/wiki/Federal_Palace_Hotel" title="Federal Palace Hotel">Federal Palace Hotel</a> and franchises of multinational chains such as Intercontinental Hotel, Sheraton and Four Points by Sheraton. Other places of interest include the <a href="/wiki/Tafawa_Balewa_Square" title="Tafawa Balewa Square">Tafawa Balewa Square</a>, Festac town, The <a href="/wiki/Nike_Art_Gallery" title="Nike Art Gallery">Nike Art Gallery</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_Park,_Lagos" title="Freedom Park, Lagos">Freedom Park, Lagos</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_Church_of_Christ,_Lagos" title="Cathedral Church of Christ, Lagos">Cathedral Church of Christ, Lagos</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_cuisine" title="Nigerian cuisine">Nigerian cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/African_cuisine" title="African cuisine">African cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg/220px-Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg/330px-Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg/440px-Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arewa_Traditional_Kitchen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Arewa Traditional Kitchen</div></div></div>
<p>Some of the famous dishes in Lagos include indigenous delicacies such as eba and egusi; amala and ewedu; <a href="/wiki/Jollof_rice" title="Jollof rice">jollof</a> (the go-to party dish); <a href="/wiki/Ofada_rice" title="Ofada rice">ofada rice</a>; plantains (locally called dodo); beans; <a href="/wiki/Suya" title="Suya">suya</a> (spicy <a href="/wiki/Shish_kebab" title="Shish kebab">shish kebab</a> or spiced roasted beef), which is consumed in local clubs and bars with a bottle of cold beer; and <a href="/wiki/Eba" title="Eba">eba</a>, made from cassava and eaten with soups prepared with vegetables and mixture of spices and herbs. Other dishes range from local ones like <i>Iyan</i> (pounded yam) made from yam flour, amala; asaro, which is usually eaten with various kind of vegetables; and <a href="/wiki/Egusi" title="Egusi">Egusi</a> (melon soup) to European, Middle-Eastern, and Asian cuisine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_161-1"><a href="#cite_note-post-161">[159]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Lagos" title="List of schools in Lagos">List of schools in Lagos</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg/220px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg/330px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg/440px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Business_School%27s_Foyer.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lagos Business School</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg/220px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg/330px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg/440px-Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lagos_Business_School%27s_Cafeteria.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lagos Business School's Cafeteria</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dowenfrontview.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dowenfrontview.jpg/220px-Dowenfrontview.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dowenfrontview.jpg/330px-Dowenfrontview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Dowenfrontview.jpg/440px-Dowenfrontview.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dowenfrontview.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dowen College in Lagos</div></div></div>
<p>The Lagos State Government operates state schools.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[186]</a></sup> The education system is the 6-3-3-4 system, which is practised throughout the country (as well as by many other members of the <a href="/wiki/Economic_Community_of_West_African_States" title="Economic Community of West African States">Economic Community of West African States</a>). The levels are Primary, Junior Secondary School (JSS), Senior Secondary School (SSS) and university. All children are offered basic education, with special focus now on the first nine years. Many of the schools in Nigeria are federally funded and usually are boarding schools. A few examples are Federal government college Odogbolu (FGCOdogbolu), Federal government girls college Sagamu (FGGCSagamu) and Federal government college Kano (FGCKano). The state of Lagos has its own federally funded high schools namely Federal government college Ijanikin also known as FGC Lagos, King's College Lagos and Queen's College Lagos.
</p><p>Lagos is home to various postsecondary schools, universities and other vocational institutions that are either operated by the government or private entities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocational_schools">Vocational schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Vocational schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_for_Industrial_Technology_(IIT)" title="Institute for Industrial Technology (IIT)">Institute for Industrial Technology (IIT)</a> : founded in 2000, IIT is a technical <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational school</a> for male youth from families with limited resources. Its educational model is based on the <a href="/wiki/Dual_education_system" title="Dual education system">Dual Training System</a>.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Polytechnics">Polytechnics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Polytechnics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Yaba_College_of_Technology" title="Yaba College of Technology">Yaba College of Technology</a> (YABATECH) : founded in 1934, the college is Nigeria's first higher educational institution and third in Africa. The college is a center of culture and heritage. Currently it has student enrolment of over 16,000.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagos_State_Polytechnic" title="Lagos State Polytechnic">Lagos State Polytechnic</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">polytechnic</a> comprising more than six schools including private polytechnics and was founded 25 years ago. Its main campus resides at Ikorodu, along Shagamu road.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lagos_City_Polytechnic" title="Lagos City Polytechnic">Lagos City Polytechnic</a>, located at 6/8, Bashiru Oweh Street, Off Simbiat Abiola Road (formerly Medical Road), Ikeja – This is the first private Polytechnic in Nigeria. It was established in 1990 by Engr. Babatunde Odufuwa. Engr. Odufuwa hails from Oke-Aye in Ijebu North East Local Government Area (I.N.E.L.G) of Ogun State.</li>
<li>Grace Polytechnic</li>
<li>Wolex Polytechnic</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Federal_College_of_Fisheries_and_Marine_Technology" title="Federal College of Fisheries and Marine Technology">Federal College of Fisheries and Marine Technology</a> is a monotechnic that offers courses in fisheries technology, general science, marine engineering and nautical science.</li>
<li>Federal College of Education (tech) Akoka</li>
<li>Ronik Polytechnic<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ronik_Polytechnic_Ejigbo_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ronik_Polytechnic_Ejigbo-190">[188]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Lagos2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="413" data-file-width="986" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/University_of_Lagos2.jpg/220px-University_of_Lagos2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/University_of_Lagos2.jpg/330px-University_of_Lagos2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/University_of_Lagos2.jpg/440px-University_of_Lagos2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:University_of_Lagos2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>University of Lagos</div></div></div>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lagos" title="University of Lagos">University of Lagos</a> (UNILAG) Akoka, is a large institution dating from 1962, with over 55,000 students. It comprises 13 faculties, run by over 4,000 staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[189]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lagos_State_University" title="Lagos State University">Lagos State University</a> (LASU) is a multi-campus university established in the year 1983 and owned by the Lagos State government. The main campus is located at Ojo, along the Lagos-Badagry Expressway.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pan-Atlantic_University" title="Pan-Atlantic University">Pan-Atlantic University</a> formerly known as Pan-African University has a business school (<a href="/wiki/Lagos_Business_School" title="Lagos Business School">LBS</a>), a school of Media and communication (SMC) and an entrepreneurial development center (EDC), specialized in providing short courses for SMEs. Lagos Business School (LBS) is the most famous of them all, awarding world-class MBA and EMBA. The School of Media and Communication is also known for its pragmatic communication courses in the field of journalism, media and marketing. SMC awards BSc., MSc., and PhD in social science courses. Founded in 1996 and awarded University status in 2002.  The university also places some emphasis on the study of <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>, running the <a href="/wiki/Virtual_Museum_of_Modern_Nigerian_Art" title="Virtual Museum of Modern Nigerian Art">Virtual Museum of Modern Nigerian Art</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Open_University_of_Nigeria" title="National Open University of Nigeria">National Open University of Nigeria</a> is the first Open university in Nigeria; it is located on Ahmadu Bello Way, Victoria Island, Lagos.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Caleb_University" title="Caleb University">Caleb University</a> is a private university located at Imota, Lagos.</li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20181227164516/http://lascohet.org/" rel="nofollow">Lagos State College of Health Technology</a> (LASCOHET) is an institution that runs health courses such as Health Information Management, Pharmacist Tech, Medical Laboratory Tech, Community Health Extension and Environmental Health Technology; it is located in Yaba.</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/College_of_Medicine,_Lagos_State_University" title="College of Medicine, Lagos State University">Lagos State University College of Medicine</a> (LASUCOM), Ikeja</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/College_of_Medicine,_University_of_Lagos" title="College of Medicine, University of Lagos">College of Medicine, University of Lagos</a> (CMUL)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Lagos" title="List of hospitals in Lagos">List of hospitals in Lagos</a></div>
<p>Lagos has many hospitals and medical facilities, some of which have accomplished feats in Nigeria's medical history. For example, the <a href="/wiki/Lagos_Island_General_Hospital" title="Lagos Island General Hospital">oldest Nigerian hospital</a> is located in the city as well as <a href="/wiki/Flying_Doctors_Nigeria" title="Flying Doctors Nigeria">West Africa's first air-operated emergency medical service</a>, which commenced in the city. The Lagos healthcare system is generally divided into public and private sectors that provide medical services at the primary, secondary, and tertiary levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[190]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Lagos" title="Transportation in Lagos">Transportation in Lagos</a></div>
<p>Lagos has one of the largest and most extensive road networks in West Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRT_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRT-194">[192]</a></sup> It also has suburban trains and some ferry services. Highways are usually <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">congested</a> in peak hours, due in part to the geography of the city, as well as to its explosive population growth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-africareport_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-africareport-106">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[193]</a></sup> Lagos is also linked by many highways and bridges.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Highways">Highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg/220px-New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg/330px-New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg/440px-New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_toll_gate_and_roads_in_Lagos_bis.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Toll gates and roads at the Lekki-Ẹpẹ Expressway</div></div></div>
<p>The Lagos–<a href="/wiki/Ibadan" title="Ibadan">Ibadan</a> Expressway and the Lagos–<a href="/wiki/Abeokuta" title="Abeokuta">Abeokuta</a> Expressway are the major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Controlled-access_highways" title="Controlled-access highways">controlled-access highways</a> in the north of the city and serve as inter-state highways to <a href="/wiki/Oyo_State" title="Oyo State">Oyo State</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ogun_State" title="Ogun State">Ogun State</a> respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[194]</a></sup> To the west the congested Lagos–Badagry Expressway serves outlying towns such as <a href="/wiki/Festac_Town" title="Festac Town"><i>Festival Town</i></a>, which was the location for the 1977 Festival of Black Arts and Culture 77.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[195]</a></sup>
</p><p>Lagos' importance as a commercial centre and port and its strategic location have led to it being the end-point of three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-African_Highway" title="Trans-African Highway">Trans-African Highway</a> routes using Nigeria's national roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[196]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Trans%E2%80%93West_African_Coastal_Highway" title="Trans–West African Coastal Highway">Trans–West African Coastal Highway</a> leaves the city as the Badagry Expressway to <a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a> and beyond as far as <a href="/wiki/Dakar" title="Dakar">Dakar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nouakchott" title="Nouakchott">Nouakchott</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Sahara_Highway" title="Trans-Sahara Highway">Trans-Sahara Highway</a> to <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, which is close to completion, leaves the city as the Lagos-Ibadan Expressway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[197]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_public_transport">Local public transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Local public transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Lagos Metropolitan Area Transport Authority (LAMATA) is responsible for public transport.
</p><p>Since 2021 using a bus or the light rail system is paid for with a public transport card without cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[198]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[199]</a></sup> This card can be used equally on BRT and LBSL buses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[200]</a></sup> One can purchase a public transportation card at any of the ticketing booths at the bus terminals scattered across Lagos State.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="City_buses">City buses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: City buses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There are two city bus companies in Lagos: BRT (<a href="/wiki/Lagos_Bus_Rapid_Transit_System" title="Lagos Bus Rapid Transit System">Lagos Bus Rapid Transit System</a>) and LBSL (Lagos Bus Services).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[202]</a></sup> The city buses are air-conditioned.
</p><p>BRT was inaugurated in 2008. BRT offers e-payment with bank cards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[203]</a></sup> On two arterial roads (Ikorodu Road and Funsho Williams Avenue), a dedicated bus lane has been established for BRT buses. BRT uses diverse brands of bus, like Ashok Leyland and Yutong. Primero Transport Services (PTS) Ltd. is the sole operator of the BRT buses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[204]</a></sup>
</p><p>LBSL was inaugurated in 2019. LBSL uses Brazilian-built Marcopolo buses.
</p><p>The central hub for city buses and long-distance buses is the <a href="/wiki/Oshodi_Bus_Terminal" title="Oshodi Bus Terminal">Oshodi Bus Terminal</a>, which is visible from afar. It is the largest bus station in West Africa and commenced operation in 2019.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Suburban_rail">Suburban rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Suburban rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Currently, a rapid transit system, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lagos_Light_Rail" title="Lagos Light Rail">Lagos Light Rail</a>, is under construction with the first section scheduled to open in 2022.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[205]</a></sup> The "Blue Line" will operate between Okokomaiko and Marina (East–west axis). The "Red Line" will run between Agbado and Marina (North–south axis).
Both lines will share three stations: Iddo, Ebute Ero and Marina.
There are plans for more light rail lines:
</p>
<ul><li>the green line (Marina to Lekki),</li>
<li>the yellow line (Otta/airport to Iddo),</li>
<li>the purple line (Redeem to Ojo),</li>
<li>the brown line (Mile 12 to Marina) and</li>
<li>the orange line (Redeem to Marina).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[206]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_transport">Rail transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Rail transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>As of 10 June 2021, Lagos has a double-track standard gauge line to Ibadan and a modern main station, Mobolaji Johnson. Departure times are 8:00 and 16:00 (on time). Ticket sales are over the counter and cash only (as of 2021). The operator is the <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_Railway_Corporation" title="Nigerian Railway Corporation">Nigerian Railway Corporation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[207]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[208]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yt_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-yt-211">[209]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[210]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Shared_cabs">Shared cabs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Shared cabs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A popular means of transportation are yellow minibuses called danfo. The yellow buses, mostly of the VW T3 or LT type, characterize the appearance of the city. They run on fixed routes, but without a timetable, according to the principle of shared cabs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[211]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ferries">Ferries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Ferries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lagos_State_Ferry_Services_Corporation" title="Lagos State Ferry Services Corporation">Lagos State Ferry Services Corporation</a> runs a few regular routes, for example between Lagos Island and the mainland, served by modern ferries and wharves. Private boats run irregular passenger services on the lagoon and on some creeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[212]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_traffic">Air traffic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Air traffic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lagos is served by <a href="/wiki/Murtala_Muhammed_International_Airport" title="Murtala Muhammed International Airport">Murtala Muhammed International Airport</a>, one of the largest and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Africa" title="List of the busiest airports in Africa">busiest airports in Africa</a>. The MMIA is Nigeria's premier international air gateway. The airport's history dates back to colonial times, around the time of the Second World War. The current international airport terminal was built and commissioned over 40 years ago, in 1978. The terminal opened officially 15 March 1979. The airport had been known simply as the Lagos International Airport. It was, however, renamed for the late Nigerian Head of State, General Murtala Muhammed, who died in 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[213]</a></sup>
</p><p>The airport terminal has been renovated several times since the 1970s but its most radical makeover began in 2013, following the launch of the Federal government's multi-billion naira Remodelling/ Rehabilitation Programme for its airports nationwide. Under the re-modeling work there, by late in 2014, the MMlA lounge area had been expanded to four times its previous size and new passenger handling conveyor systems installed which can handle over 1,000 passengers per hour.
</p><p>A second airport, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lekki-Epe_International_Airport" title="Lekki-Epe International Airport">Lekki-Epe International Airport</a> is proposed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logistics_hub">Logistics hub</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Logistics hub">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="849" data-file-width="1135" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png/220px-Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png/330px-Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png/440px-Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ketu-Ereyun_logistics_park.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logistics hub, close to Epe</div></div></div>
<p>In Ketu-Ereyun, between <a href="/wiki/Epe,_Lagos_State" title="Epe, Lagos State">Epe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ikorodu" title="Ikorodu">Ikorodu</a>, Lagos State builds a "<a href="/wiki/Food_Logistics_Park_Lagos" title="Food Logistics Park Lagos">Food Logistics Park</a>" - the biggest logistics hub for food in Sub-Saharan Africa. The site is 1.2 million square metres big and the construction is expected to be finished in 2024.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timber_trade">Timber trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Timber trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the middle of the city, in the Oko Baba district, there is (as of September 2022) a large transhipment centre for timber, mainly <a href="/wiki/Sequoioideae" title="Sequoioideae">redwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">mahogany</a>. This timber trade, including sawmill, will move to a new location, "<a href="/wiki/Timberville_(Lagos)" title="Timberville (Lagos)">Timberville</a>", in December 2022.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Kenny_Adeleke" title="Kenny Adeleke">Kenny Adeleke</a> (born 1983), basketball player<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[227]</a></sup></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Oyinkan_Braithwaite" title="Oyinkan Braithwaite">Oyinkan Braithwaite</a>, novelist and writer, who wrote <i><a href="/wiki/My_Sister,_the_Serial_Killer" title="My Sister, the Serial Killer">My Sister, the Serial Killer</a></i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agbani_Darego" title="Agbani Darego">Agbani Darego</a>, Miss Nigeria 2001, Semifinalist Miss Universe 2001 and Miss World 2001<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[236]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Buchi_Emecheta" title="Buchi Emecheta">Buchi Emecheta</a>, novelist<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[238]</a></sup></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Esther_Uzodinma" title="Esther Uzodinma">Esther Uzodinma</a>, actress and producer</li></ul>
<h2><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_–_sister_cities">Twin towns – sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Lagos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Twin towns – sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Africa#Nigeria" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Africa">List of twin towns and sister cities in Nigeria</a></div>
<p>Lagos is <a href="/wiki/Sister_city" title="Sister city">twinned</a> with:
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, United States<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[240]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" decoding="async" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Gary,_Indiana" title="Gary, Indiana">Gary, Indiana</a>, United States</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil"><img alt="Brazil" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="720" decoding="async" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/22px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/33px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/05/Flag_of_Brazil.svg/43px-Flag_of_Brazil.svg.png 2x" width="22"/></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Belo_Horizonte" title="Belo Horizonte">Belo Horizonte</a>, Brazil<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[241]</a></sup></li>

<li id="cite_note-159"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-159">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 1995, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> stated that "70 percent of Lagos' population lived in <a href="/wiki/Squatting_in_Nigeria" title="Squatting in Nigeria">squatted</a> settlements in extremely poor environmental surroundings. Knee-deep floods sweeping raw sewage and refuse inside densely packed homes were frequent in neighborhoods where overcrowding was the norm. While the average residential density for Lagos was about 260 people per hectare, the population density in slums was between 790 and 1240 people per hectare." <a class="external text" href="http://documents.worldbank.org/curated/en/872021468290442515/pdf/ICR29680P071340IC0disclosed04040140.pdf" rel="nofollow">Nigeria - Lagos Metropolitan Development and Governance Project</a>, report of World Bank, 2006 (lookup on 2016-11-23)</span>
